               \n                    Zoe Leverant                \n            \n                                    Perhaps it’s because they got together in college instead of high school, but Philly pop punkers Modern Baseball are a lot more mature than other bands of their ilk. Switching between crunchy power strumming and thoughtful melodic guitar work, their songs cover territory that’s familiar and make it sound new. By employing every member of the four-piece for vocals, choruses that would normally feel worn-out become vital, and typically teenage concerns like crushes and general ennui take on a more serious note. It helps that the singers never fall into the affected sneer common in their genre, opting instead to borrow pop-punk’s best qualities—lust for life, satisfying chords, passionate songwriting—and repurpose them into an uncanny (and superior) version of the same sound. After a long break, they returned to the studio last year to record Holy Ghost, which arrives in early summer, when the band finally graduates from Drexel University.
